responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \\\"compact\\\" retention strategy.\\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\\n52:  * <p>\\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \\\"clean\\\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\\n54:  * \\\"dirty\\\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \\\"cleanable\\\" section followed by an \\\"uncleanable\\\" section.\\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\\n57:  * <p>\\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \\\"compact\\\" retention policy\\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\\n60:  * <p>\\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\\n63:  * <p>\\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\\n69:  * <p>\\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\\n71:  * <p>\\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\\n82:  * are the key points:\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * <ol>\\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\\n96:  * </ol>\\n97:  */\\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\\n99:     private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\\n100: \\n101:     public static final Set<String> RECONFIGURABLE_CONFIGS = Set.of(\\n102:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_THREADS_PROP,\\n103: CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\\n106:             ServerConfigs.MESSAGE_MAX_BYTES_CONFIG,\\n107:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_MAX_BYTES_PER_SECOND_PROP,\\n108:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_BACKOFF_MS_PROP\\n109:     );\\n110: \\n111:     // Visible for test\\n112:     public static final String MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"max-buffer-utilization-percent\\\";\\n113:     public static final String MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME = \\\"max-clean-time-secs\\\";\\n114:     public static final String MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME = \\\"max-compaction-delay-secs\\\";\\n115: \\n116:     private static final String CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"cleaner-recopy-percent\\\";\\n117:     private static final String DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"DeadThreadCount\\\";\\n118: \\n119:     // Visible for test\\n120:     public static final Set<String> METRIC_NAMES = Set.of(\\n121:             MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n122:             CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n123:             MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME,\\n124: \"Kafka's log compaction architecture is implemented in the apache/kafka repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489). The implementation consists of three main components:\\n\\n**1. Cleaner Thread (LogCleaner.java):**\\nThe LogCleaner class is the main orchestrator for log cleaning. It implements BrokerReconfigurable and manages a pool of CleanerThread instances. Each CleanerThread (nested class extending ShutdownableThread) runs in the background, selecting the dirtiest log partitions with compact cleanup policy and performing cleaning operations. The LogCleaner class is located at storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java and contains the CleanerThread nested class.\\n\\n**2. Segment Selection Policy (LogCleanerManager.java):**\\nThe segment selection policy is implemented in LogCleanerManager (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java). The key methods are:\\n- grabFilthiestCompactedLog(): Selects the dirtiest log for cleaning based on the cleanable ratio (dirty bytes / total bytes)\\n- cleanableOffsets(): Determines which offsets in a log can be cleaned, respecting compaction lag constraints (minCleanableRatio, compactionLagMs, maxCompactionLagMs)\\nThe class also manages OffsetsToClean records and PreCleanStats for tracking cleaning progress.\\n\\n**3. Key-Based Deduplication Logic (Cleaner.java):**\\nThe core deduplication logic is in the Cleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/Cleaner.java). The key methods are:\\n- buildOffsetMap(): Creates a key=>offset mapping (OffsetMap) for all messages in the dirty section. This is the foundation for deduplication.\\n- buildOffsetMapForSegment(): Builds the offset map segment by segment, using SkimpyOffsetMap as the implementation.\\n- shouldRetainRecord(): The critical deduplication decision method. For each message, it checks:\\n  * If the message's offset is newer than the latest offset for that key in the map, retain it\\n  * If the message has a value, retain it\\n  * If the message is a tombstone (null value), check if it's past the delete horizon before discarding\\n- cleanInto(): Performs the actual cleaning of segments using a RecordFilter that applies the shouldRetainRecord logic\\n- cleanSegments(): Orchestrates cleaning of multiple segments, handling transaction metadata and producer state preservation\\n\\nSupporting classes include:\\n- OffsetMap/SkimpyOffsetMap: Hash-based key=>offset deduplication maps\\n- LogToClean: Represents a partition eligible for cleaning with metrics\\n- CleanedTransactionMetadata: Tracks aborted transactions and control batch state during cleaning\\n- LogConfig: Contains compaction configuration like deleteRetentionMs, minCleanableRatio, compactionLagMs\\n- UnifiedLog: The main log structure with methods like lastRecordsOfActiveProducers() used to preserve producer state\\n\\nThe compaction workflow: LogCleaner schedules CleanerThreads → select log via grabFilthiestCompactedLog() → build OffsetMap via buildOffsetMap() → clean segments via cleanSegments() → filter messages via cleanInto()/shouldRetainRecord() → preserve only latest versions of keys.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7552,"cache_read_input_tokens":90167,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":7552},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"82ff39c0-81fc-4609-a0b0-38a54b1fba92","uuid":"5104d494-f028-4233-b4aa-7ab37ead08d6"}
